$$-0.0884v^3 - 0.1959v\sin(x) - 3.998x^3 - 0.1959\sin(v)$$

The key terms are:
1. $-3.998x^3$ (polynomial in x)
2. $-0.0884v^3$ (polynomial in v)
3. $-0.1959v\sin(x)$ (mixed term with sin(x))
4. $-0.1959\sin(v)$ (nonlinear in v)

No candidate has both $v\sin(x)$ and $\sin(v)$ terms. In fact, only candidate 11 has $v\sin(x)$ type term, but none have $\sin(v)$.

Let me reconsider whether any combination of non-sinusoidal terms could approximate $\sin(v)$ exactly. Since $\sin(v)$ is transcendental and the candidates offer polynomials, absolute values, exponentials, and logarithms of $v$, none can exactly equal $\sin(v)$ for all $v$.

Similarly, $v\sin(x)$ cannot be exactly represented by combinations of $vx$, $vx^2$, $vx^3$, $v|x|$, $v\exp(cx)$, $x/(c+x)$, $x^2\log(cx^2+1)$, etc., for all $x$.

The only way to get exact equivalence would be if some candidate contained both $\sin(v)$ and $v\sin(x)$ terms (or equivalent). None do.

Let me double-check candidate 11 more carefully: `c0*x/(c1 + x) + c2*v*x**2 + c3*x**3 + c4*v + c5*v**3 + c6*v*x + c7*v*sin(c8*x + c9)`. This has $v\sin(c_8 x + c_9)$ which can give $v\sin(x)$, but still needs $\sin(v)$ which isn't available.

No candidate contains a $\sin(v)$ term or any sinusoidal function of $v$.

[NO MATCH]
